<step>
[Core idea]: We start by applying the change-of-base formula for logarithms to rewrite the equation.
[Full step]: The change-of-base formula for logarithms states that for any positive real numbers a, b, and c, and for any a ≠ 1, b ≠ 1, c ≠ 1: $\log_{a}c = \frac{\log_{b}c}{\log_{b}a}$. We can use this formula to rewrite the given equation using a common base. Let's use the natural logarithm (base e) as our common base. Applying the change-of-base formula to each term, we get: $\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}$. We simplify the equation by canceling out the common factors of ln 2023 in the numerators and denominators of the fractions on both sides.
</step>

Since $\ln (289x) = \ln (17^2x) = 2\ln 17 + \ln x$ and $\ln (7x) = \ln 7 + \ln x$, we can substitute these expressions back into our equation to get the equation in terms of natural logarithms.

 After canceling out the common factors of ln 2023, the equation becomes: $\frac{1}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{1}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{1}{\ln (2023x)}$. Simplifying this equation, we can multiply both sides by the product of the denominators to eliminate the fractions. This results in $(\ln (7x))(\ln (289x))=(\ln (2023x))$. We then apply the property of logarithms that states $\log_{a}b\cdot\log_{b}c = \log_{a}c$. This allows us to rewrite the equation as $\ln (7x\cdot 289x)=\ln (2023x)$. Simplifying the left-hand side gives us $\ln (2023\cdot 7x^2) = \ln (2023x)$. Since the natural logarithm function is one-to-one, we can equate the expressions inside the logarithms, resulting in $2023\cdot 7x^2 = 2023x$. Now we have an algebraic equation that we can solve for x.

 We simplify the equation further by multiplying the fractions on the left-hand side, which yields: \[\frac{(\ln 2023)^2}{\ln (7x)\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}.\] Then, we can rewrite the equation as \[(\ln 2023)^2 = \ln (2023x) \cdot \ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x).\] Now, we use the property of logarithms that $\log_a b = \log_b b^a$, which allows us to rewrite $\ln 2023 = \ln 2023^1. Now the equation looks like this: \[ \ln (2023^2) = \ln (2023x)\ln (7x)\ln (289x).\] Next, we apply the property of logarithms that $\log_a b + \log_a c = \log_a (bc)$ to combine the right-hand side of the equation: \[\ln (2023^2) = \ln ((2023x)^{\ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x)}).\] Taking the exponential of both sides of the equation gives: \[2023^2 = (2023x)^{\ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x)}.\] Now, we can see that we have an exponential equation, and we can solve for x by isolating x on one side of the equation.

[Full step]: The change-of-base formula for logarithms states that for any positive real numbers a, b, and c, and for any a ≠ 1, b ≠ 1, c ≠ 1: $\log_{a}c = \frac{\log_{b}c}{\log_{b}a}$. [Full step]: We simplify the equation further by multiplying the fractions on the left-hand side, which yields: \[\frac{(\ln 2023)^2}{\ln (7x)\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}.\] Then, we can rewrite the equation as \[(\ln 2023)^2 = \ln (2023x) \cdot \ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x).\] Now, we use the property of logarithms that $\log_a b = \log_b b^a$, which allows us to rewrite $\ln 2023 = \ln 2023^1. Question: What is the product of all solutions to the equation
\[\log_{7x}2023\cdot \log_{289x}2023=\log_{2023x}2023\]

Step 1: <step>
[Core idea]: We start by applying the change-of-base formula for logarithms to rewrite the equation.
[Full step]: The change-of-base formula for logarithms states that for any positive real numbers a, b, and c, and for any a ≠ 1, b ≠ 1, c ≠ 1: $\log_{a}c = \frac{\log_{b}c}{\log_{b}a}$. We can use this formula to rewrite the given equation using a common base. Let's use the natural logarithm (base e) as our common base. Applying the change-of-base formula to each term, we get: $\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}$. We simplify the equation by canceling out the common factors of ln 2023 in the numerators and denominators of the fractions on both sides.
</step>
Step 2: <step>
[Core idea]: Simplify the resulting equation by using properties of logarithms to combine the fractions and potentially isolate the variable x.
[Full step]: After canceling out the common factors of ln 2023, the equation becomes: $\frac{1}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{1}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{1}{\ln (2023x)}$. Simplifying this equation, we can multiply both sides by the product of the denominators to eliminate the fractions. This results in $(\ln (7x))(\ln (289x))=(\ln (2023x))$. We then apply the property of logarithms that states $\log_{a}b\cdot\log_{b}c = \log_{a}c$. This allows us to rewrite the equation as $\ln (7x\cdot 289x)=\ln (2023x)$. Simplifying the left-hand side gives us $\ln (2023\cdot 7x^2) = \ln (2023x)$. Since the natural logarithm function is one-to-one, we can equate the expressions inside the logarithms, resulting in $2023\cdot 7x^2 = 2023x$. Now we have an algebraic equation that we can solve for x.
</step>

Step 1: <step>

[Full step]: The change-of-base formula for logarithms states that for any positive real numbers a, b, and c, and for any a ≠ 1, b ≠ 1, c ≠ 1: $\log_{a}c = \frac{\log_{b}c}{\log_{b}a}$. We can use this formula to rewrite the given equation using a common base. Let's use the natural logarithm (base e) as our common base. Applying the change-of-base formula to each term, we get: $\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}$. We simplify the equation by canceling out the common factors of ln 2023 in the numerators and denominators of the fractions on both sides.
</step>
Step 2: <step>
[Core idea]: Apply the property that if a^b = c then b = log_a(c) to rewrite the equation in a form where we can easily solve for x.
[Full step]: We can rewrite the equation as $\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}$ which can be rewritten as $\frac{(\ln 2023)^2}{\ln (7x)\ln (289x)} = \frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}$. Since $\ln (289x) = \ln (17^2x) = 2\ln 17 + \ln x$ and $\ln (7x) = \ln 7 + \ln x$, we can substitute these expressions back into our equation to get the equation in terms of natural logarithms.

Question: What is the product of all solutions to the equation
\[\log_{7x}2023\cdot \log_{289x}2023=\log_{2023x}2023\]

Step 1: <step>
[Core idea]: We start by applying the change-of-base formula for logarithms to rewrite the equation.
[Full step]: The change-of-base formula for logarithms states that for any positive real numbers a, b, and c, and for any a ≠ 1, b ≠ 1, c ≠ 1: $\log_{a}c = \frac{\log_{b}c}{\log_{b}a}$. We can use this formula to rewrite the given equation using a common base. Let's use the natural logarithm (base e) as our common base. Applying the change-of-base formula to each term, we get: $\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}$. We simplify the equation by canceling out the common factors of ln 2023 in the numerators and denominators of the fractions on both sides.
</step>
Step 2: <step>
[Core idea]: Simplify the resulting equation by using properties of logarithms to combine the fractions and potentially isolate the variable x.
[Full step]: After canceling out the common factors of ln 2023, the equation becomes: $\frac{1}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{1}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{1}{\ln (2023x)}$. Simplifying this equation, we can multiply both sides by the product of the denominators to eliminate the fractions. This results in $(\ln (7x))(\ln (289x))=(\ln (2023x))$. We then apply the property of logarithms that states $\log_{a}b\cdot\log_{b}c = \log_{a}c$. This allows us to rewrite the equation as $\ln (7x\cdot 289x)=\ln (2023x)$. Simplifying the left-hand side gives us $\ln (2023\cdot 7x^2) = \ln (2023x)$. Since the natural logarithm function is one-to-one, we can equate the expressions inside the logarithms, resulting in $2023\cdot 7x^2 = 2023x$. Now we have an algebraic equation that we can solve for x.
</step>

\[\log_{7x}2023\cdot \log_{289x}2023=\log_{2023x}2023\]

Step 1: <step>
[Core idea]: We start by applying the change-of-base formula for logarithms to rewrite the equation.
[Full step]: The change-of-base formula for logarithms states that for any positive real numbers a, b, and c, and for any a ≠ 1, b ≠ 1, c ≠ 1: $\log_{a}c = \frac{\log_{b}c}{\log_{b}a}$. We can use this formula to rewrite the given equation using a common base. Let's use the natural logarithm (base e) as our common base. Applying the change-of-base formula to each term, we get: $\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}$. We simplify the equation by canceling out the common factors of ln 2023 in the numerators and denominators of the fractions on both sides.
</step>
Step 2: <step>
[Core idea]: Simplify the resulting equation by using properties of logarithms to combine the fractions and potentially isolate the variable x.
[Full step]: After canceling out the common factors of ln 2023, the equation becomes: $\frac{1}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{1}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{1}{\ln (2023x)}$. Simplifying this equation, we can multiply both sides by the product of the denominators to eliminate the fractions. This results in $(\ln (7x))(\ln (289x))=(\ln (2023x))$. We then apply the property of logarithms that states $\log_{a}b\cdot\log_{b}c = \log_{a}c$. This allows us to rewrite the equation as $\ln (7x\cdot 289x)=\ln (2023x)$. Simplifying the left-hand side gives us $\ln (2023\cdot 7x^2) = \ln (2023x)$. Since the natural logarithm function is one-to-one, we can equate the expressions inside the logarithms, resulting in $2023\cdot 7x^2 = 2023x$. Now we have an algebraic equation that we can solve for x.
</step>

Step 1: <step>
[Core idea]: We start by applying the change-of-base formula for logarithms to rewrite the equation.
[Full step]: The change-of-base formula for logarithms states that for any positive real numbers a, b, and c, and for any a ≠ 1, b ≠ 1, c ≠ 1: $\log_{a}c = \frac{\log_{b}c}{\log_{b}a}$. We can use this formula to rewrite the given equation using a common base. Let's use the natural logarithm (base e) as our common base. Applying the change-of-base formula to each term, we get: $\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}$. We simplify the equation by canceling out the common factors of ln 2023 in the numerators and denominators of the fractions on both sides.

[Core idea]: Simplify the resulting equation by using properties of logarithms to combine the fractions and potentially isolate the variable x.
[Full step]: After canceling out the common factors of ln 2023, the equation becomes: $\frac{1}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{1}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{1}{\ln (2023x)}$. Simplifying this equation, we can multiply both sides by the product of the denominators to eliminate the fractions. This results in $(\ln (7x))(\ln (289x))=(\ln (2023x))$. Simplifying the left-hand side gives us $\ln (2023\cdot 7x^2) = \ln (2023x)$. Since the natural logarithm function is one-to-one, we can equate the expressions inside the logarithms, resulting in $2023\cdot 7x^2 = 2023x$. Now we have an algebraic equation that we can solve for x.
</step>

[Core idea]: Focus on the equality of the expressions inside the logarithms, leading to a comparison of the product of the arguments of the logarithms.

Question: What is the product of all solutions to the equation
\[\log_{7x}2023\cdot \log_{289x}2023=\log_{2023x}2023\]

Step 1: <step>
[Core idea]: We start by applying the change-of-base formula for logarithms to rewrite the equation.
[Full step]: The change-of-base formula for logarithms states that for any positive real numbers a, b, and c, and for any a ≠ 1, b ≠ 1, c ≠ 1: $\log_{a}c = \frac{\log_{b}c}{\log_{b}a}$. We can use this formula to rewrite the given equation using a common base. Let's use the natural logarithm (base e) as our common base. Applying the change-of-base formula to each term, we get: $\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}$. We simplify the equation by canceling out the common factors of ln 2023 in the numerators and denominators of the fractions on both sides.
</step>
Step 2: <step>
[Core idea]: Simplify the resulting equation by using properties of logarithms to combine the fractions and potentially isolate the variable x.
[Full step]: After canceling out the common factors of ln 2023, the equation becomes: $\frac{1}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{1}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{1}{\ln (2023x)}$. Simplifying this equation, we can multiply both sides by the product of the denominators to eliminate the fractions. This results in $(\ln (7x))(\ln (289x))=(\ln (2023x))$. We then apply the property of logarithms that states $\log_{a}b\cdot\log_{b}c = \log_{a}c$. This allows us to rewrite the equation as $\ln (7x\cdot 289x)=\ln (2023x)$. Simplifying the left-hand side gives us $\ln (2023\cdot 7x^2) = \ln (2023x)$. Since the natural logarithm function is one-to-one, we can equate the expressions inside the logarithms, resulting in $2023\cdot 7x^2 = 2023x$. Now we have an algebraic equation that we can solve for x.
</step>
Step 3: <step>
[Core idea]: Use properties of logarithms to combine the terms and eliminate the logarithms, resulting in a simplified equation.
[Full step]: Simplifying the equation, we have $\ln (2023\cdot 7x^2) = \ln (2023x)$. Since the natural logarithm function is one-to-one, we can equate the expressions inside the logarithms. Therefore, $2023\cdot 7x^2 = 2023x$. To simplify this equation, we can start by dividing both sides by 2023, which gives us $7x^2 = x$. Next, we can subtract x from both sides to get $6x^2 = 0$. We can factor out x from the left-hand side, resulting in $x(6x) = 0$. This tells us that either $x = 0$ or $6x = 0$. Solving for x in both cases, we find that $x = 0$ or $x = 0$. However, we need to consider the domain of the logarithmic functions in the original equation. Since the base of a logarithm must be positive and not equal to 1, we know that $7x > 0$ and $289x > 0$. Therefore, x must be positive. Hence, the solution to the equation is x = 0.

Question: What is the product of all solutions to the equation
\[\log_{7x}2023\cdot \log_{289x}2023=\log_{2023x}2023\]

Step 1: <step>
[Core idea]: We start by applying the change-of-base formula for logarithms to rewrite the equation.
[Full step]: The change-of-base formula for logarithms states that for any positive real numbers a, b, and c, and for any a ≠ 1, b ≠ 1, c ≠ 1: $\log_{a}c = \frac{\log_{b}c}{\log_{b}a}$. We can use this formula to rewrite the given equation using a common base. Let's use the natural logarithm (base e) as our common base. Applying the change-of-base formula to each term, we get: $\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}$. We simplify the equation by canceling out the common factors of ln 2023 in the numerators and denominators of the fractions on both sides.
</step>
Step 2: <step>
[Core idea]: Simplify the resulting equation by using properties of logarithms to combine the fractions and potentially isolate the variable x.
[Full step]: After canceling out the common factors of ln 2023, the equation becomes: $\frac{1}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{1}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{1}{\ln (2023x)}$. Simplifying this equation, we can multiply both sides by the product of the denominators to eliminate the fractions. This results in $(\ln (7x))(\ln (289x))=(\ln (2023x))$. We then apply the property of logarithms that states $\log_{a}b\cdot\log_{b}c = \log_{a}c$. This allows us to rewrite the equation as $\ln (7x\cdot 289x)=\ln (2023x)$. Simplifying the left-hand side gives us $\ln (2023\cdot 7x^2) = \ln (2023x)$. Since the natural logarithm function is one-to-one, we can equate the expressions inside the logarithms, resulting in $2023\cdot 7x^2 = 2023x$. Now we have an algebraic equation that we can solve for x.
</step>
Step 3: <step>
[Core idea]: Focus on the equality of the expressions inside the logarithms, leading to a comparison of the product of the arguments of the logarithms.
[Full step]: We begin by equating the expressions inside the logarithms: $2023\cdot 7x^2 = 2023x$. We can simplify this equation by first factoring out the common factor of 2023 from both sides. This yields $2023(7x^2) = 2023x$. The factor 2023 cancels out on both sides, leaving us with $7x^2 = x$. Now we have a quadratic equation in x. To isolate x, we can rearrange the equation by subtracting x from both sides, giving us $7x^2 - x = 0$. We can then factor out x from both terms, resulting in $x(7x - 1) = 0$. This is a product of two factors, and we can set each factor equal to zero to find the possible solutions for x. Therefore, we have the equation $x = 0$ or $7x - 1 = 0$. We can solve each of these equations for x by isolating the variable. For the first equation, we have $x = 0$. For the second equation, we add 1 to both sides to get $7x = 1$, and then divide both sides by 7 to get $x = \frac{1}{7}$.
</step>

For the second equation, we add 1 to both sides to get $7x = 1$, and then divide both sides by 7 to get $x = \frac{1}{7}$.
</step>

We simplify the expression further by canceling out the common factors in the numerators and denominators of the fractions on both sides. Question: What is the product of all solutions to the equation
\[\log_{7x}2023\cdot \log_{289x}2023=\log_{2023x}2023\]

Step 1: <step>
[Core idea]: We start by applying the change-of-base formula for logarithms to rewrite the equation.
[Full step]: The change-of-base formula for logarithms states that for any positive real numbers a, b, and c, and for any a ≠ 1, b ≠ 1, c ≠ 1: $\log_{a}c = \frac{\log_{b}c}{\log_{b}a}$. We can use this formula to rewrite the given equation using a common base. Let's use the natural logarithm (base e) as our common base. Applying the change-of-base formula to each term, we get: $\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}$. We simplify the equation by canceling out the common factors of ln 2023 in the numerators and denominators of the fractions on both sides.
</step>
Step 2: <step>
[Core idea]: Use the properties of logarithms and exponents to rewrite the equation in terms of powers of x and solve for x.
[Full step]: We simplify the equation further by multiplying the fractions on the left-hand side, which yields: \[\frac{(\ln 2023)^2}{\ln (7x)\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}.\] Then, we can rewrite the equation as \[(\ln 2023)^2 = \ln (2023x) \cdot \ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x).\] Now, we use the property of logarithms that $\log_a b = \log_b b^a$, which allows us to rewrite $\ln 2023 = \ln 2023^1. Now the equation looks like this: \[ \ln (2023^2) = \ln (2023x)\ln (7x)\ln (289x).\] Next, we apply the property of logarithms that $\log_a b + \log_a c = \log_a (bc)$ to combine the right-hand side of the equation: \[\ln (2023^2) = \ln ((2023x)^{\ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x)}).\] Taking the exponential of both sides of the equation gives: \[2023^2 = (2023x)^{\ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x)}.\] Now, we can see that we have an exponential equation, and we can solve for x by isolating x on one side of the equation.
</step>

[Core idea]: We can rewrite the equation as \[2 = \ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x) \cdot \ln x.\] Using the property of logarithms that $\log_a b \cdot \log_a c = \log_a (b^c)$, we can rewrite the equation as \[2 = \ln x^{\ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x)}.\] Now, we can equate the exponents of $x$ on both sides of the equation, since the bases are the same. This gives us the equation \[1 = 17x.\] Solving for x, we get \[x = \frac{1}{17}.\] Therefore, the product of all solutions to the equation is \[7^{\frac{1}{17}} \cdot 289^{\frac{1}{17}} \cdot 2023^{\frac{1}{17}} = 2023^{\frac{1}{17}} \cdot 7^{\frac{1}{17}} \cdot 17^{\frac{2}{17}} \cdot 2023^{\frac{1}{17}}.\]
</step>

[Full step]: Looking at the equation $2023^2 = (2023x)^{\ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x)}$, we can use the fact that two expressions are equal if and only if their exponents are equal. This gives us the equation $\ln (7x)\ln (289x) = 2$ because $2023^2$ is equal to $2023^2$ raised to the power of 1 and we know that $(x^a)^b = x^{a\cdot b}$, where x, a, and b are arbitrary real numbers. Furthermore, we can simplify the left-hand side of this equation using the logarithmic property $a\cdot b = 2$, $\log_b a + \log_b c = \log_b (ac)$ and $a \cdot b = b \cdot a$, which gives us $\log_{289} 7 + \log_{289} x = 2$. Question: What is the product of all solutions to the equation
\[\log_{7x}2023\cdot \log_{289x}2023=\log_{2023x}2023\]

Step 1: <step>
[Core idea]: We start by applying the change-of-base formula for logarithms to rewrite the equation.
[Full step]: The change-of-base formula for logarithms states that for any positive real numbers a, b, and c, and for any a ≠ 1, b ≠ 1, c ≠ 1: $\log_{a}c = \frac{\log_{b}c}{\log_{b}a}$. We can use this formula to rewrite the given equation using a common base. Let's use the natural logarithm (base e) as our common base. Applying the change-of-base formula to each term, we get: $\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}$. We simplify the equation by canceling out the common factors of ln 2023 in the numerators and denominators of the fractions on both sides.
</step>
Step 2: <step>
[Core idea]: Use the properties of logarithms and exponents to rewrite the equation in terms of powers of x and solve for x.
[Full step]: We simplify the equation further by multiplying the fractions on the left-hand side, which yields: \[\frac{(\ln 2023)^2}{\ln (7x)\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}.\] Then, we can rewrite the equation as \[(\ln 2023)^2 = \ln (2023x) \cdot \ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x).\] Now, we use the property of logarithms that $\log_a b = \log_b b^a$, which allows us to rewrite $\ln 2023 = \ln 2023^1. Now the equation looks like this: \[ \ln (2023^2) = \ln (2023x)\ln (7x)\ln (289x).\] Next, we apply the property of logarithms that $\log_a b + \log_a c = \log_a (bc)$ to combine the right-hand side of the equation: \[\ln (2023^2) = \ln ((2023x)^{\ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x)}).\] Taking the exponential of both sides of the equation gives: \[2023^2 = (2023x)^{\ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x)}.\] Now, we can see that we have an exponential equation, and we can solve for x by isolating x on one side of the equation.
</step>
Step 3: <step>
[Core idea]: Use the property of logarithms to rewrite the equation in a form that allows for the direct comparison of exponents.
[Full step]: We can rewrite the equation as \[2023^2 = (2023x)^{\ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x)}.\] Using the property of logarithms that $\log_a b = \log_b b^a$, we can rewrite the right-hand side of the equation as \[2023^2 = 2023^{\ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x) \cdot \ln x}.\] Now, we can equate the exponents of 2023 on both sides of the equation, since the bases are the same. This gives us the equation \[2 = \ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x) \cdot \ln x.\]
</step>

</step>
Step 2: <step>
[Core idea]: Apply the property that if a^b = c then b = log_a(c) to rewrite the equation in a form where we can easily solve for x.
[Full step]: We can rewrite the equation as $\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}$ which can be rewritten as $\frac{(\ln 2023)^2}{\ln (7x)\ln (289x)} = \frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}$. Since $\ln (289x) = \ln (17^2x) = 2\ln 17 + \ln x$ and $\ln (7x) = \ln 7 + \ln x$, we can substitute these expressions back into our equation to get the equation in terms of natural logarithms. 


The final answer to the question is \boxed{7}
</step>
</think>

Question: What is the product of all solutions to the equation
\[\log_{7x}2023\cdot \log_{289x}2023=\log_{2023x}2023\]

Step 1: <step>
[Core idea]: We start by applying the change-of-base formula for logarithms to rewrite the equation.
[Full step]: The change-of-base formula for logarithms states that for any positive real numbers a, b, and c, and for any a ≠ 1, b ≠ 1, c ≠ 1: $\log_{a}c = \frac{\log_{b}c}{\log_{b}a}$. We can use this formula to rewrite the given equation using a common base. Let's use the natural logarithm (base e) as our common base. Applying the change-of-base formula to each term, we get: $\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}$. We simplify the equation by canceling out the common factors of ln 2023 in the numerators and denominators of the fractions on both sides.
</step>
Step 2: <step>
[Core idea]: Simplify the resulting equation by using properties of logarithms to combine the fractions and potentially isolate the variable x.
[Full step]: After canceling out the common factors of ln 2023, the equation becomes: $\frac{1}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{1}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{1}{\ln (2023x)}$. Simplifying this equation, we can multiply both sides by the product of the denominators to eliminate the fractions. This results in $(\ln (7x))(\ln (289x))=(\ln (2023x))$. We then apply the property of logarithms that states $\log_{a}b\cdot\log_{b}c = \log_{a}c$. This allows us to rewrite the equation as $\ln (7x\cdot 289x)=\ln (2023x)$. Simplifying the left-hand side gives us $\ln (2023\cdot 7x^2) = \ln (2023x)$. Since the natural logarithm function is one-to-one, we can equate the expressions inside the logarithms, resulting in $2023\cdot 7x^2 = 2023x$. Now we have an algebraic equation that we can solve for x.
</step>
Step 3: <step>
[Core idea]: Distribute the product on the left side of the equation and simplify to get a quadratic equation in terms of x.
[Full step]: We begin by distributing the 2023 to the terms inside the parentheses on the left-hand side of the equation: $2023\cdot 7x^2 = 2023x$. We can simplify this by canceling out the common factor of 2023. This results in $7x^2 = x$. We can further simplify by factoring out an x from both terms on the left-hand side, yielding $x(7x - 1) = 0$. This is a quadratic equation in x, and we can solve for x by setting each factor equal to zero.
</step>

 Given the equation $x(7x - 1) = 0$, we can use the zero-product property, which states that if the product of two or more factors is zero, then at least one of the factors must be zero. We can apply this property to our equation. We have two factors: $x$ and $(7x - 1)$. Since their product is zero, we can set each factor equal to zero and solve for x. Setting $x = 0$ gives us the solution $x = 0$. Setting $7x - 1 = 0$ gives us the quadratic equation $7x - 1 = 0$. Solving for x in this equation, we add 1 to both sides, resulting in $7x = 1$. Finally, we divide both sides by 7 to find $x = \frac{1}{7}$.

 We can rearrange the equation $x(7x-1)=0$ into a standard quadratic equation form, which is $7x^2 - x = 0$. To solve for x, we can use the quadratic formula $x = \frac{-b\pm\sqrt{b^2-4ac}}{2a}$, where a, b, and c are the coefficients of the quadratic equation. For the quadratic equation $7x^2 - x = 0$, a = 7, b = -1, and c = 0. Substituting these values into the quadratic formula, we get $x = \frac{-(-1)\pm\sqrt{(-1)^2-4(7)(0)}}{2(7)}$. This simplifies to $x = \frac{1\pm\sqrt{1}}{14}$. Therefore, we have two possible values for x: $x = \frac{1+\sqrt{1}}{14}$ and $x = \frac{1-\sqrt{1}}{14}$. Since $\sqrt{1}=1$, this simplifies to $x = \frac{1+1}{14}$ and $x = \frac{1-1}{14}$. This leads to $x = \frac{2}{14}$ and $x = \frac{0}{14}$, which simplifies to $x = \frac{1}{7}$ and $x = 0$.

[Core idea]: We start by applying the change-of-base formula for logarithms to rewrite the equation.
[Full step]: The change-of-base formula for logarithms states that for any positive real numbers a, b, and c, and for any a ≠ 1, b ≠ 1, c ≠ 1: $\log_{a}c = \frac{\log_{b}c}{\log_{b}a}$. We can use this formula to rewrite the given equation using a common base. Let's use the natural logarithm (base e) as our common base. Applying the change-of-base formula to each term, we get: $\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}$. We simplify the equation by canceling out the common factors of ln 2023 in the numerators and denominators of the fractions on both sides.
</step>
Step 2: <step>
[Core idea]: Simplify the resulting equation by using properties of logarithms to combine the fractions and potentially isolate the variable x.
[Full step]: After canceling out the common factors of ln 2023, the equation becomes: $\frac{1}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{1}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{1}{\ln (2023x)}$. Simplifying this equation, we can multiply both sides by the product of the denominators to eliminate the fractions. This results in $(\ln (7x))(\ln (289x))=(\ln (2023x))$. We then apply the property of logarithms that states $\log_{a}b\cdot\log_{b}c = \log_{a}c$. This allows us to rewrite the equation as $\ln (7x\cdot 289x)=\ln (2023x)$. Simplifying the left-hand side gives us $\ln (2023\cdot 7x^2) = \ln (2023x)$. Since the natural logarithm function is one-to-one, we can equate the expressions inside the logarithms, resulting in $2023\cdot 7x^2 = 2023x$. Now we have an algebraic equation that we can solve for x.
</step>
Step 3: <step>
[Core idea]: Distribute the product on the left side of the equation and simplify to get a quadratic equation in terms of x.
[Full step]: We begin by distributing the 2023 to the terms inside the parentheses on the left-hand side of the equation: $2023\cdot 7x^2 = 2023x$. We can simplify this by canceling out the common factor of 2023. This results in $7x^2 = x$. We can further simplify by factoring out an x from both terms on the left-hand side, yielding $x(7x - 1) = 0$. This is a quadratic equation in x, and we can solve for x by setting each factor equal to zero.
</step>
Step 4: <step>
[Core idea]: Apply the zero-product property directly, as one of the factors is already zero, to find the solution for x.
[Full step]: Given the equation $x(7x - 1) = 0$, we can use the zero-product property, which states that if the product of two or more factors is zero, then at least one of the factors must be zero. We can apply this property to our equation. We have two factors: $x$ and $(7x - 1)$. Since their product is zero, we can set each factor equal to zero and solve for x. Setting $x = 0$ gives us the solution $x = 0$. Setting $7x - 1 = 0$ gives us the quadratic equation $7x - 1 = 0$. Solving for x in this equation, we add 1 to both sides, resulting in $7x = 1$. Finally, we divide both sides by 7 to find $x = \frac{1}{7}$.
</step>

For the quadratic equation $7x^2 - x = 0$, a = 7, b = -1, and c = 0. Substituting these values into the quadratic formula, we get $x = \frac{-(-1)\pm\sqrt{(-1)^2-4(7)(0)}}{2(7)}$. This simplifies to $x = \frac{1\pm\sqrt{1}}{14}$. Therefore, we have two possible values for x: $x = \frac{1+\sqrt{1}}{14}$ and $x = \frac{1-\sqrt{1}}{14}$. Since $\sqrt{1}=1$, this simplifies to $x = \frac{1+1}{14}$ and $x = \frac{1-1}{14}$. This leads to $x = \frac{2}{14}$ and $x = \frac{0}{14}$, which simplifies to $x = \frac{1}{7}$ and $x = 0$.

[Full step]: The change-of-base formula for logarithms states that for any positive real numbers a, b, and c, and for any a ≠ 1, b ≠ 1, c ≠ 1: $\log_{a}c = \frac{\log_{b}c}{\log_{b}a}$. We can use this formula to rewrite the given equation using a common base. Let's use the natural logarithm (base e) as our common base. Applying the change-of-base formula to each term, we get: $\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}$. We simplify the equation by canceling out the common factors of ln 2023 in the numerators and denominators of the fractions on both sides.
</step>
Step 2: <step>
[Core idea]: Simplify the resulting equation by using properties of logarithms to combine the fractions and potentially isolate the variable x.
[Full step]: After canceling out the common factors of ln 2023, the equation becomes: $\frac{1}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{1}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{1}{\ln (2023x)}$. Simplifying this equation, we can multiply both sides by the product of the denominators to eliminate the fractions. This results in $(\ln (7x))(\ln (289x))=(\ln (2023x))$. We then apply the property of logarithms that states $\log_{a}b\cdot\log_{b}c = \log_{a}c$. This allows us to rewrite the equation as $\ln (7x\cdot 289x)=\ln (2023x)$. Simplifying the left-hand side gives us $\ln (2023\cdot 7x^2) = \ln (2023x)$. Since the natural logarithm function is one-to-one, we can equate the expressions inside the logarithms, resulting in $2023\cdot 7x^2 = 2023x$. Now we have an algebraic equation that we can solve for x.
</step>
Step 3: <step>
[Core idea]: Distribute the product on the left side of the equation and simplify to get a quadratic equation in terms of x.
[Full step]: We begin by distributing the 2023 to the terms inside the parentheses on the left-hand side of the equation: $2023\cdot 7x^2 = 2023x$. We can simplify this by canceling out the common factor of 2023. This results in $7x^2 = x$. We can further simplify by factoring out an x from both terms on the left-hand side, yielding $x(7x - 1) = 0$. This is a quadratic equation in x, and we can solve for x by setting each factor equal to zero.
</step>
Step 4: <step>
[Core idea]: Factor the quadratic equation and solve for x by considering the product of the factors equal to zero.
[Full step]: The equation we obtained is $x(7x - 1) = 0$. This is a quadratic equation in x, and we can solve for x by setting each factor equal to zero. To find the solutions to this equation, we need to set each factor equal to zero and solve for x. The first factor is x, and setting $x = 0$ gives us one solution. The second factor is $7x - 1$, and setting $7x - 1 = 0$ gives us the quadratic equation $7x - 1 = 0$. We can solve this equation for x by adding 1 to both sides, resulting in $7x = 1$. Then, we can divide both sides by 7 to get $x = \frac{1}{7}$. These are the two solutions to the equation $x(7x - 1) = 0$.


The final answer to the question is \boxed{0, 1/7}

Applying the change-of-base formula to each term, we get: $\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}$. We simplify the equation by canceling out the common factors of ln 2023 in the numerators and denominators of the fractions on both sides.
</step>
Step 2: <step>
[Core idea]: Simplify the resulting equation by using properties of logarithms to combine the fractions and potentially isolate the variable x.
[Full step]: After canceling out the common factors of ln 2023, the equation becomes: $\frac{1}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{1}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{1}{\ln (2023x)}$. Simplifying this equation, we can multiply both sides by the product of the denominators to eliminate the fractions. This results in $(\ln (7x))(\ln (289x))=(\ln (2023x))$. We then apply the property of logarithms that states $\log_{a}b\cdot\log_{b}c = \log_{a}c$. This allows us to rewrite the equation as $\ln (7x\cdot 289x)=\ln (2023x)$. Simplifying the left-hand side gives us $\ln (2023\cdot 7x^2) = \ln (2023x)$. </step>
Step 4: <step>

[Full step]: We can rearrange the equation $x(7x-1)=0$ into a standard quadratic equation form, which is $7x^2 - x = 0$. To solve for x, we can use the quadratic formula $x = \frac{-b\pm\sqrt{b^2-4ac}}{2a}$, where a, b, and c are the coefficients of the quadratic equation. For the quadratic equation $7x^2 - x = 0$, a = 7, b = -1, and c = 0. Substituting these values into the quadratic formula, we get $x = \frac{-(-1)\pm\sqrt{(-1)^2-4(7)(0)}}{2(7)}$. This simplifies to $x = \frac{1\pm\sqrt{1}}{14}$. Therefore, we have two possible values for x: $x = \frac{1+\sqrt{1}}{14}$ and $x = \frac{1-\sqrt{1}}{14}$. Since $\sqrt{1}=1$, this simplifies to $x = \frac{1+1}{14}$ and $x = \frac{1-1}{14}$. This leads to $x = \frac{2}{14}$ and $x = \frac{0}{14}$, which simplifies to $x = \frac{1}{7}$ and $x = 0$.


The final answer to the question is \boxed{\frac{1}

We then apply the property of logarithms that states $\log_{a}b\cdot\log_{b}c = \log_{a}c$. This allows us to rewrite the equation as $\ln (7x\cdot 289x)=\ln (2023x)$. Simplifying the left-hand side gives us $\ln (2023\cdot 7x^2) = \ln (2023x)$. Since the natural logarithm function is one-to-one, we can equate the expressions inside the logarithms, resulting in $2023\cdot 7x^2 = 2023x$. Now we have an algebraic equation that we can solve for x.
</step>
Step 3: <step>
[Core idea]: Distribute the product on the left side of the equation and simplify to get a quadratic equation in terms of x.
[Full step]: We begin by distributing the 2023 to the terms inside the parentheses on the left-hand side of the equation: $2023\cdot 7x^2 = 2023x$. We can simplify this by canceling out the common factor of 2023. This results in $7x^2 = x$. We can further simplify by factoring out an x from both terms on the left-hand side, yielding $x(7x - 1) = 0$. This is a quadratic equation in x, and we can solve for x by setting each factor equal to zero.
</step>
Step 4: <step>
[Core idea]: Factor the quadratic equation and solve for x by considering the product of the factors equal to zero.
[Full step]: The equation we obtained is $x(7x - 1) = 0$. This is a quadratic equation in x, and we can solve for x by setting each factor equal to zero. To find the solutions to this equation, we need to set each factor equal to zero and solve for x. The first factor is x, and setting $x = 0$ gives us one solution. The second factor is $7x - 1$, and setting $7x - 1 = 0$ gives us the quadratic equation $7x - 1 = 0$. We can solve this equation for x by adding 1 to both sides, resulting in $7x = 1$. Then, we can divide both sides by 7 to get $x = \frac{1}{7}$. These are the two solutions to the equation $x(7x - 1) = 0$.


The final answer to the question is \boxed{0, 1/7}
</step>

[Full step]: We simplify the equation further by multiplying the fractions on the left-hand side, which yields: \[\frac{(\ln 2023)^2}{\ln (7x)\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}.\] Then, we can rewrite the equation as \[(\ln 2023)^2 = \ln (2023x) \cdot \ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x).\] Now, we use the property of logarithms that $\log_a b = \log_b b^a$, which allows us to rewrite $\ln 2023 = \ln 2023^1. </step>

[Full step]: We can rewrite the equation as \[2023^2 = (2023x)^{\ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x)}.\] Using the property of logarithms that $\log_a b = \log_b b^a$, we can rewrite the right-hand side of the equation as \[2023^2 = 2023^{\ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x) \cdot \ln x}.\] Now, we can equate the exponents of 2023 on both sides of the equation, since the bases are the same.  We can rewrite the equation as \[2 = \ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x) \cdot \ln x.\] By the AM-GM inequality, we have: \[\frac{\ln (7x) + \ln (289x) + \ln x}{3} \ge \sqrt[3]{\ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x) \cdot \ln x}.\] Since \[\ln (7x) + \ln (289x) + \ln x = \ln (7x \cdot 289x \cdot x) = \ln (7x)^3 = 3\ln (7x),\] we have \[3\ln (7x) \ge 2,\] which implies \[\ln (7x) \ge 2/3.\] Now, we can substitute this back into the original equation and simplify. Step 2: <step>
[Core idea]: Use the properties of logarithms and exponents to rewrite the equation in terms of powers of x and solve for x.
[Full step]: We simplify the equation further by multiplying the fractions on the left-hand side, which yields: \[\frac{(\ln 2023)^2}{\ln (7x)\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}.\] Then, we can rewrite the equation as \[(\ln 2023)^2 = \ln (2023x) \cdot \ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x).\] Now, we use the property of logarithms that $\log_a b = \log_b b^a$, which allows us to rewrite $\ln 2023 = \ln 2023^1. Now the equation looks like this: \[ \ln (2023^2) = \ln (2023x)\ln (7x)\ln (289x).\] Next, we apply the property of logarithms that $\log_a b + \log_a c = \log_a (bc)$ to combine the right-hand side of the equation: \[\ln (2023^2) = \ln ((2023x)^{\ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x)}).\] Taking the exponential of both sides of the equation gives: \[2023^2 = (2023x)^{\ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x)}.\] Now, we can see that we have an exponential equation, and we can solve for x by isolating x on one side of the equation.
</step>
Step 3: <step>
[Core idea]: Use the property of logarithms to rewrite the equation in a form that allows for the direct comparison of exponents.
[Full step]: We can rewrite the equation as \[2023^2 = (2023x)^{\ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x)}.\] Using the property of logarithms that $\log_a b = \log_b b^a$, we can rewrite the right-hand side of the equation as \[2023^2 = 2023^{\ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x) \cdot \ln x}.\] Now, we can equate the exponents of 2023 on both sides of the equation, since the bases are the same. This gives us the equation \[2 = \ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x) \cdot \ln x.\]
</step>
Step 4: <step>
[Core idea]: Use the properties of logarithms to simplify the equation further by combining logarithms and applying power reduction formulas.
[Full step]: We can rewrite the equation as \[2 = \ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x) \cdot \ln x.\] Using the property of logarithms that $\log_a b \cdot \log_b c = \log_a c$, we can simplify the equation to \[2 = \ln (289x^2) \cdot \ln x.\] Now, we can use the power reduction formula for logarithms, $\log_a b^c = c \log_a b$, to rewrite $\ln(289x^2)$ as $\ln 289 + \ln x^2$. This gives us the equation \[2 = (\ln 289 + 2\ln x) \cdot \ln x.\] We can expand the right-hand side of the equation to get \[2 = \ln 289 \cdot \ln x + 2(\ln x)^2.\] Now, we have a quadratic equation in terms of $\ln x$.
</step>

Question: What is the product of all solutions to the equation
\[\log_{7x}2023\cdot \log_{289x}2023=\log_{2023x}2023\]

Step 1: <step>
[Core idea]: We start by applying the change-of-base formula for logarithms to rewrite the equation.
[Full step]: The change-of-base formula for logarithms states that for any positive real numbers a, b, and c, and for any a ≠ 1, b ≠ 1, c ≠ 1: $\log_{a}c = \frac{\log_{b}c}{\log_{b}a}$. We can use this formula to rewrite the given equation using a common base. Let's use the natural logarithm (base e) as our common base. Applying the change-of-base formula to each term, we get: $\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}$. We simplify the equation by canceling out the common factors of ln 2023 in the numerators and denominators of the fractions on both sides.
</step>
Step 2: <step>
[Core idea]: Use the properties of logarithms and exponents to rewrite the equation in terms of powers of x and solve for x.
[Full step]: We simplify the equation further by multiplying the fractions on the left-hand side, which yields: \[\frac{(\ln 2023)^2}{\ln (7x)\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}.\] Then, we can rewrite the equation as \[(\ln 2023)^2 = \ln (2023x) \cdot \ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x).\] Now, we use the property of logarithms that $\log_a b = \log_b b^a$, which allows us to rewrite $\ln 2023 = \ln 2023^1. Now the equation looks like this: \[ \ln (2023^2) = \ln (2023x)\ln (7x)\ln (289x).\] Next, we apply the property of logarithms that $\log_a b + \log_a c = \log_a (bc)$ to combine the right-hand side of the equation: \[\ln (2023^2) = \ln ((2023x)^{\ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x)}).\] Taking the exponential of both sides of the equation gives: \[2023^2 = (2023x)^{\ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x)}.\] Now, we can see that we have an exponential equation, and we can solve for x by isolating x on one side of the equation.
</step>
Step 3: <step>
[Core idea]: Use the property of logarithms to rewrite the equation in a form that allows for the direct comparison of exponents.
[Full step]: We can rewrite the equation as \[2023^2 = (2023x)^{\ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x)}.\] Using the property of logarithms that $\log_a b = \log_b b^a$, we can rewrite the right-hand side of the equation as \[2023^2 = 2023^{\ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x) \cdot \ln x}.\] Now, we can equate the exponents of 2023 on both sides of the equation, since the bases are the same. This gives us the equation \[2 = \ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x) \cdot \ln x.\]
</step>
Step 4: <step>
[Core idea]: Use the properties of logarithms to simplify the equation further by combining logarithms and applying power reduction formulas.
[Full step]: We can rewrite the equation as \[2 = \ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x) \cdot \ln x.\] Using the property of logarithms that $\log_a b \cdot \log_b c = \log_a c$, we can simplify the equation to \[2 = \ln (289x^2) \cdot \ln x.\] Now, we can use the power reduction formula for logarithms, $\log_a b^c = c \log_a b$, to rewrite $\ln(289x^2)$ as $\ln 289 + \ln x^2$. This gives us the equation \[2 = (\ln 289 + 2\ln x) \cdot \ln x.\] We can expand the right-hand side of the equation to get \[2 = \ln 289 \cdot \ln x + 2(\ln x)^2.\] Now, we have a quadratic equation in terms of $\ln x$.
</step>

Question: What is the product of all solutions to the equation
\[\log_{7x}2023\cdot \log_{289x}2023=\log_{2023x}2023\]

Step 1: <step>
[Core idea]: We start by applying the change-of-base formula for logarithms to rewrite the equation.
[Full step]: The change-of-base formula for logarithms states that for any positive real numbers a, b, and c, and for any a ≠ 1, b ≠ 1, c ≠ 1: $\log_{a}c = \frac{\log_{b}c}{\log_{b}a}$. We can use this formula to rewrite the given equation using a common base. Let's use the natural logarithm (base e) as our common base. Applying the change-of-base formula to each term, we get: $\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}$. We simplify the equation by canceling out the common factors of ln 2023 in the numerators and denominators of the fractions on both sides.
</step>
Step 2: <step>
[Core idea]: Simplify the resulting equation by using properties of logarithms to combine the fractions and potentially isolate the variable x.
[Full step]: After canceling out the common factors of ln 2023, the equation becomes: $\frac{1}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{1}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{1}{\ln (2023x)}$. Simplifying this equation, we can multiply both sides by the product of the denominators to eliminate the fractions. This results in $(\ln (7x))(\ln (289x))=(\ln (2023x))$. We then apply the property of logarithms that states $\log_{a}b\cdot\log_{b}c = \log_{a}c$. This allows us to rewrite the equation as $\ln (7x\cdot 289x)=\ln (2023x)$. Simplifying the left-hand side gives us $\ln (2023\cdot 7x^2) = \ln (2023x)$. Since the natural logarithm function is one-to-one, we can equate the expressions inside the logarithms, resulting in $2023\cdot 7x^2 = 2023x$. Now we have an algebraic equation that we can solve for x.
</step>
Step 3: <step>
[Core idea]: Focus on the equality of the expressions inside the logarithms, leading to a comparison of the product of the arguments of the logarithms.
[Full step]: We begin by equating the expressions inside the logarithms: $2023\cdot 7x^2 = 2023x$. We can simplify this equation by first factoring out the common factor of 2023 from both sides. This yields $2023(7x^2) = 2023x$. The factor 2023 cancels out on both sides, leaving us with $7x^2 = x$. Now we have a quadratic equation in x. To isolate x, we can rearrange the equation by subtracting x from both sides, giving us $7x^2 - x = 0$. We can then factor out x from both terms, resulting in $x(7x - 1) = 0$. This is a product of two factors, and we can set each factor equal to zero to find the possible solutions for x. Therefore, we have the equation $x = 0$ or $7x - 1 = 0$. We can solve each of these equations for x by isolating the variable. For the first equation, we have $x = 0$. For the second equation, we add 1 to both sides to get $7x = 1$, and then divide both sides by 7 to get $x = \frac{1}{7}$.
</step>

Question: What is the product of all solutions to the equation
\[\log_{7x}2023\cdot \log_{289x}2023=\log_{2023x}2023\]

Step 1: <step>
[Core idea]: We start by applying the change-of-base formula for logarithms to rewrite the equation.
[Full step]: The change-of-base formula for logarithms states that for any positive real numbers a, b, and c, and for any a ≠ 1, b ≠ 1, c ≠ 1: $\log_{a}c = \frac{\log_{b}c}{\log_{b}a}$. We can use this formula to rewrite the given equation using a common base. Let's use the natural logarithm (base e) as our common base. Applying the change-of-base formula to each term, we get: $\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}$. We simplify the equation by canceling out the common factors of ln 2023 in the numerators and denominators of the fractions on both sides.
</step>
Step 2: <step>
[Core idea]: Simplify the resulting equation by using properties of logarithms to combine the fractions and potentially isolate the variable x.
[Full step]: After canceling out the common factors of ln 2023, the equation becomes: $\frac{1}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{1}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{1}{\ln (2023x)}$. Simplifying this equation, we can multiply both sides by the product of the denominators to eliminate the fractions. This results in $(\ln (7x))(\ln (289x))=(\ln (2023x))$. We then apply the property of logarithms that states $\log_{a}b\cdot\log_{b}c = \log_{a}c$. This allows us to rewrite the equation as $\ln (7x\cdot 289x)=\ln (2023x)$. Simplifying the left-hand side gives us $\ln (2023\cdot 7x^2) = \ln (2023x)$. Since the natural logarithm function is one-to-one, we can equate the expressions inside the logarithms, resulting in $2023\cdot 7x^2 = 2023x$. Now we have an algebraic equation that we can solve for x.
</step>
Step 3: <step>
[Core idea]: Focus on the equality of the expressions inside the logarithms, leading to a comparison of the product of the arguments of the logarithms.
[Full step]: We begin by equating the expressions inside the logarithms: $2023\cdot 7x^2 = 2023x$. We can simplify this equation by first factoring out the common factor of 2023 from both sides. This yields $2023(7x^2) = 2023x$. The factor 2023 cancels out on both sides, leaving us with $7x^2 = x$. Now we have a quadratic equation in x. To isolate x, we can rearrange the equation by subtracting x from both sides, giving us $7x^2 - x = 0$. We can then factor out x from both terms, resulting in $x(7x - 1) = 0$. This is a product of two factors, and we can set each factor equal to zero to find the possible solutions for x. Therefore, we have the equation $x = 0$ or $7x - 1 = 0$. We can solve each of these equations for x by isolating the variable. For the first equation, we have $x = 0$. For the second equation, we add 1 to both sides to get $7x = 1$, and then divide both sides by 7 to get $x = \frac{1}{7}$.
</step>

We can use this formula to rewrite the given equation using a common base. Let's use the natural logarithm (base e) as our common base. Applying the change-of-base formula to each term, we get: $\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}$. We simplify the equation by canceling out the common factors of ln 2023 in the numerators and denominators of the fractions on both sides.
</step>
Step 2: <step>
[Core idea]: Simplify the resulting equation by using properties of logarithms to combine the fractions and potentially isolate the variable x.
[Full step]: After canceling out the common factors of ln 2023, the equation becomes: $\frac{1}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{1}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{1}{\ln (2023x)}$. Simplifying this equation, we can multiply both sides by the product of the denominators to eliminate the fractions. This results in $(\ln (7x))(\ln (289x))=(\ln (2023x))$. We then apply the property of logarithms that states $\log_{a}b\cdot\log_{b}c = \log_{a}c$. This allows us to rewrite the equation as $\ln (7x\cdot 289x)=\ln (2023x)$. Simplifying the left-hand side gives us $\ln (2023\cdot 7x^2) = \ln (2023x)$. Since the natural logarithm function is one-to-one, we can equate the expressions inside the logarithms, resulting in $2023\cdot 7x^2 = 2023x$. Now we have an algebraic equation that we can solve for x.
</step>
Step 3: <step>
[Core idea]: Focus on the equality of the expressions inside the logarithms, leading to a comparison of the product of the arguments of the logarithms.
[Full step]: We begin by equating the expressions inside the logarithms: $2023\cdot 7x^2 = 2023x$. We can simplify this equation by first factoring out the common factor of 2023 from both sides. This yields $2023(7x^2) = 2023x$. The factor 2023 cancels out on both sides, leaving us with $7x^2 = x$. Now we have a quadratic equation in x. To isolate x, we can rearrange the equation by subtracting x from both sides, giving us $7x^2 - x = 0$. We can then factor out x from both terms, resulting in $x(7x - 1) = 0$. This is a product of two factors, and we can set each factor equal to zero to find the possible solutions for x. Therefore, we have the equation $x = 0$ or $7x - 1 = 0$. We can solve each of these equations for x by isolating the variable. For the first equation, we have $x = 0$. For the second equation, we add 1 to both sides to get $7x = 1$, and then divide both sides by 7 to get $x = \frac{1}{7}$.
</step>
Step 4: <step>
[Core idea]: Consider using algebraic manipulation to solve for x, such as adding x to both sides and factoring to find a quadratic equation.
[Full step]: Now that we have the equation $x(7x - 1) = 0$, we can proceed to solve for x. We have two cases to consider: $x = 0$ and $7x - 1 = 0$. Let's start with the first case, $x = 0$. In this case, it's clear that x is 0. Now let's consider the second case, $7x - 1 = 0$. We can add 1 to both sides to get $7x = 1$. Then, we can divide both sides by 7 to solve for x, giving us $x = \frac{1}{7}$.


The final answer to the question is \boxed{0, 1/7}
</step>

[Full step]: After canceling out the common factors of ln 2023, the equation becomes: $\frac{1}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{1}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{1}{\ln (2023x)}$. Simplifying this equation, we can multiply both sides by the product of the denominators to eliminate the fractions. This results in $(\ln (7x))(\ln (289x))=(\ln (2023x))$. We then apply the property of logarithms that states $\log_{a}b\cdot\log_{b}c = \log_{a}c$. This allows us to rewrite the equation as $\ln (7x\cdot 289x)=\ln (2023x)$. Simplifying the left-hand side gives us $\ln (2023\cdot 7x^2) = \ln (2023x)$. Since the natural logarithm function is one-to-one, we can equate the expressions inside the logarithms, resulting in $2023\cdot 7x^2 = 2023x$. Now we have an algebraic equation that we can solve for x.
</step>
Step 3: <step>
[Core idea]: Focus on the equality of the expressions inside the logarithms, leading to a comparison of the product of the arguments of the logarithms.
[Full step]: We begin by equating the expressions inside the logarithms: $2023\cdot 7x^2 = 2023x$. We can simplify this equation by first factoring out the common factor of 2023 from both sides. This yields $2023(7x^2) = 2023x$. The factor 2023 cancels out on both sides, leaving us with $7x^2 = x$. Now we have a quadratic equation in x. To isolate x, we can rearrange the equation by subtracting x from both sides, giving us $7x^2 - x = 0$. We can then factor out x from both terms, resulting in $x(7x - 1) = 0$. This is a product of two factors, and we can set each factor equal to zero to find the possible solutions for x. Therefore, we have the equation $x = 0$ or $7x - 1 = 0$. We can solve each of these equations for x by isolating the variable. For the first equation, we have $x = 0$. For the second equation, we add 1 to both sides to get $7x = 1$, and then divide both sides by 7 to get $x = \frac{1}{7}$.
</step>
Step 4: <step>
[Core idea]: Factor out the common factor from the equation $7x^2 - x = 0$ to simplify and find possible solutions for x.
[Full step]: We can factor out x from both terms of the equation $7x^2 - x = 0$. This gives us $x(7x - 1) = 0$. This factorization is obtained by finding the greatest common factor of the two terms, which in this case is x. Factoring out x allows us to rewrite the equation in a more compact form and potentially find solutions for x. By setting each factor equal to zero, we can find the possible solutions for x. We have two factors: $x = 0$ and $7x - 1 = 0$. We can solve each of these equations for x separately.

Question: What is the product of all solutions to the equation
\[\log_{7x}2023\cdot \log_{289x}2023=\log_{2023x}2023\]

Step 1: <step>
[Core idea]: We start by applying the change-of-base formula for logarithms to rewrite the equation.
[Full step]: The change-of-base formula for logarithms states that for any positive real numbers a, b, and c, and for any a ≠ 1, b ≠ 1, c ≠ 1: $\log_{a}c = \frac{\log_{b}c}{\log_{b}a}$. We can use this formula to rewrite the given equation using a common base. Let's use the natural logarithm (base e) as our common base. Applying the change-of-base formula to each term, we get: $\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}$. We simplify the equation by canceling out the common factors of ln 2023 in the numerators and denominators of the fractions on both sides.
</step>
Step 2: <step>
[Core idea]: Apply the property that if a^b = c then b = log_a(c) to rewrite the equation in a form where we can easily solve for x.
[Full step]: We can rewrite the equation as $\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}$ which can be rewritten as $\frac{(\ln 2023)^2}{\ln (7x)\ln (289x)} = \frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}$. Since $\ln (289x) = \ln (17^2x) = 2\ln 17 + \ln x$ and $\ln (7x) = \ln 7 + \ln x$, we can substitute these expressions back into our equation to get the equation in terms of natural logarithms. 


The final answer to the question is \boxed{7}

[Full step]: The change-of-base formula for logarithms states that for any positive real numbers a, b, and c, and for any a ≠ 1, b ≠ 1, c ≠ 1: $\log_{a}c = \frac{\log_{b}c}{\log_{b}a}$. We can use this formula to rewrite the given equation using a common base. Let's use the natural logarithm (base e) as our common base. Applying the change-of-base formula to each term, we get: $\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}$. We simplify the equation by canceling out the common factors of ln 2023 in the numerators and denominators of the fractions on both sides.
</step>
Step 2: <step>
[Core idea]: Simplify the resulting equation by using properties of logarithms to combine the fractions and potentially isolate the variable x.
[Full step]: After canceling out the common factors of ln 2023, the equation becomes: $\frac{1}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{1}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{1}{\ln (2023x)}$. Simplifying this equation, we can multiply both sides by the product of the denominators to eliminate the fractions. This results in $(\ln (7x))(\ln (289x))=(\ln (2023x))$. We then apply the property of logarithms that states $\log_{a}b\cdot\log_{b}c = \log_{a}c$. This allows us to rewrite the equation as $\ln (7x\cdot 289x)=\ln (2023x)$. Simplifying the left-hand side gives us $\ln (2023\cdot 7x^2) = \ln (2023x)$. Since the natural logarithm function is one-to-one, we can equate the expressions inside the logarithms, resulting in $2023\cdot 7x^2 = 2023x$. Now we have an algebraic equation that we can solve for x.
</step>
Step 3: <step>
[Core idea]: Distribute the product on the left side of the equation and simplify to get a quadratic equation in terms of x.
[Full step]: We begin by distributing the 2023 to the terms inside the parentheses on the left-hand side of the equation: $2023\cdot 7x^2 = 2023x$. We can simplify this by canceling out the common factor of 2023. This results in $7x^2 = x$. We can further simplify by factoring out an x from both terms on the left-hand side, yielding $x(7x - 1) = 0$. This is a quadratic equation in x, and we can solve for x by setting each factor equal to zero.
</step>
Step 4: <step>
[Core idea]: Factor the quadratic equation and solve for x by considering the product of the factors equal to zero.
[Full step]: The equation we obtained is $x(7x - 1) = 0$. This is a quadratic equation in x, and we can solve for x by setting each factor equal to zero. To find the solutions to this equation, we need to set each factor equal to zero and solve for x. The first factor is x, and setting $x = 0$ gives us one solution. The second factor is $7x - 1$, and setting $7x - 1 = 0$ gives us the quadratic equation $7x - 1 = 0$. We can solve this equation for x by adding 1 to both sides, resulting in $7x = 1$. Then, we can divide both sides by 7 to get $x = \frac{1}{7}$. These are the two solutions to the equation $x(7x - 1) = 0$.


The final answer to the question is \boxed{0, 1/7}
</step>

\[\log_{7x}2023\cdot \log_{289x}2023=\log_{2023x}2023\]

[Core idea]: We start by applying the change-of-base formula for logarithms to rewrite the equation.
[Full step]: The change-of-base formula for logarithms states that for any positive real numbers a, b, and c, and for any a ≠ 1, b ≠ 1, c ≠ 1: $\log_{a}c = \frac{\log_{b}c}{\log_{b}a}$. We can use this formula to rewrite the given equation using a common base. Let's use the natural logarithm (base e) as our common base. Applying the change-of-base formula to each term, we get: $\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}$. We simplify the equation by canceling out the common factors of ln 2023 in the numerators and denominators of the fractions on both sides.
</step>
Step 2: <step>
[Core idea]: Simplify the resulting equation by using properties of logarithms to combine the fractions and potentially isolate the variable x.
[Full step]: After canceling out the common factors of ln 2023, the equation becomes: $\frac{1}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{1}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{1}{\ln (2023x)}$. Simplifying this equation, we can multiply both sides by the product of the denominators to eliminate the fractions. This results in $(\ln (7x))(\ln (289x))=(\ln (2023x))$. We then apply the property of logarithms that states $\log_{a}b\cdot\log_{b}c = \log_{a}c$. This allows us to rewrite the equation as $\ln (7x\cdot 289x)=\ln (2023x)$. Step 4: <step>

[Full step]: We can rearrange the equation $x(7x-1)=0$ into a standard quadratic equation form, which is $7x^2 - x = 0$. To solve for x, we can use the quadratic formula $x = \frac{-b\pm\sqrt{b^2-4ac}}{2a}$, where a, b, and c are the coefficients of the quadratic equation. For the quadratic equation $7x^2 - x = 0$, a = 7, b = -1, and c = 0. Substituting these values into the quadratic formula, we get $x = \frac{-(-1)\pm\sqrt{(-1)^2-4(7)(0)}}{2(7)}$. This simplifies to $x = \frac{1\pm\sqrt{1}}{14}$. Therefore, we have two possible values for x: $x = \frac{1+\sqrt{1}}{14}$ and $x = \frac{1-\sqrt{1}}{14}$. \[\log_{7x}2023\cdot \log_{289x}2023=\log_{2023x}2023\]

Step 1: <step>
[Core idea]: We start by applying the change-of-base formula for logarithms to rewrite the equation.
[Full step]: The change-of-base formula for logarithms states that for any positive real numbers a, b, and c, and for any a ≠ 1, b ≠ 1, c ≠ 1: $\log_{a}c = \frac{\log_{b}c}{\log_{b}a}$. We can use this formula to rewrite the given equation using a common base. Let's use the natural logarithm (base e) as our common base. Applying the change-of-base formula to each term, we get: $\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}$. We simplify the equation by canceling out the common factors of ln 2023 in the numerators and denominators of the fractions on both sides.
</step>
Step 2: <step>
[Core idea]: Use the properties of logarithms and exponents to rewrite the equation in terms of powers of x and solve for x.
[Full step]: We simplify the equation further by multiplying the fractions on the left-hand side, which yields: \[\frac{(\ln 2023)^2}{\ln (7x)\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}.\] Then, we can rewrite the equation as \[(\ln 2023)^2 = \ln (2023x) \cdot \ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x).\] Now, we use the property of logarithms that $\log_a b = \log_b b^a$, which allows us to rewrite $\ln 2023 = \ln 2023^1. Now the equation looks like this: \[ \ln (2023^2) = \ln (2023x)\ln (7x)\ln (289x).\] Next, we apply the property of logarithms that $\log_a b + \log_a c = \log_a (bc)$ to combine the right-hand side of the equation: \[\ln (2023^2) = \ln ((2023x)^{\ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x)}).\] Taking the exponential of both sides of the equation gives: \[2023^2 = (2023x)^{\ln (7x) \cdot \ln (289x)}.\] Now, we can see that we have an exponential equation, and we can solve for x by isolating x on one side of the equation.
</step>
Step 3: <step>
[Core idea]: Apply the change-of-base formula in a different way, such as using a different base or combining logarithms with properties of logarithms.
[Full step]:  Let's apply the change-of-base formula using base 2023 for all the logarithms. This will give us $\frac{\log_{7x}2023}{\log_{7x}2023}\cdot\frac{\log_{289x}2023}{\log_{289x}2023}=\frac{\log_{2023x}2023}{\log_{2023x}2023}$. Since $\frac{\log_{a}a}{\log_{a}b}=1$, the equation simplifies to $1\cdot1=1$. This simplification is not helpful for solving for x. Let's try a different approach. We can use the property of logarithms that $\log_{a}b=\frac{\log b}{\log a}$ to rewrite the equation as $\frac{\frac{\log 2023}{\log (7x)}}{\frac{\log 2023}{\log (7x)}}\cdot\frac{\frac{\log 2023}{\log (289x)}}{\frac{\log 2023}{\log (289x)}}=\frac{\frac{\log 2023}{\log (2023x)}}{\frac{\log 2023}{\log (2023x)}}$. Canceling out the common factors in the numerator and denominator of each fraction, we get $1\cdot1=1$. This is not helpful for solving for x. We need to find a different way to simplify the equation. We can combine the logarithms on the left-hand side using the property of logarithms that $\log_{a}b + \log_{a}c = \log_{a}(b\cdot c)$. This gives us $\frac{\log 2023}{\log (7x)}+\frac{\log 2023}{\log (289x)}=\frac{\log 2023}{\log (2023x)}$. We can combine the fractions on the left-hand side by finding a common denominator: $\frac{\log 2023\cdot \log(289x)+\log 2023\cdot \log (7x)}{\log (7x)\log (289x)}=\frac{\log 2023}{\log (2023x)}$. The $\log 2023$ terms in the numerator cancel out, giving us $\frac{\log(289x)+\log (7x)}{\
</step>
Step 4: <step>
[Core idea]: Apply logarithmic properties to combine the fractions on the left-hand side of the equation.
[Full step]: We simplify the given equation by combining the fractions using the property of logarithms that $\frac{a}{b}+\frac{c}{d}=\frac{ad+bc}{bd}$. Applying this property to the left-hand side of the equation, we get \[\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (7x)} \cdot \frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln (2023x) \cdot \ln (289x) + \ln (2023) \cdot \ln (7x)}{\ln (7x) \ln (289x)}.\] We can factor out $\ln 2023$ from the numerator, giving us \[\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (7x)} \cdot \frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (289x)} = \frac{\ln 2023 (\ln (289x) + \ln (7x))}{\ln (7x) \ln (289x)}.\] The numerator can be simplified using the property of logarithms that $\log_a b + \log_a c = \log_a (bc)$, which gives us \[\frac{\ln 2023 (\ln (289x \cdot 7x))}{\ln (7x) \ln (289x)} = \frac{\ln 2023 (\ln (2023x^2))}{\ln (7x) \ln (289x)}.\]
</step>

\[\log_{7x}2023\cdot \log_{289x}2023=\log_{2023x}2023\]

Step 1: <step>
[Core idea]: We start by applying the change-of-base formula for logarithms to rewrite the equation.
[Full step]: The change-of-base formula for logarithms states that for any positive real numbers a, b, and c, and for any a ≠ 1, b ≠ 1, c ≠ 1: $\log_{a}c = \frac{\log_{b}c}{\log_{b}a}$. We can use this formula to rewrite the given equation using a common base. Let's use the natural logarithm (base e) as our common base. Applying the change-of-base formula to each term, we get: $\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}$. \[\log_{7x}2023\cdot \log_{289x}2023=\log_{2023x}2023\]

Step 1: <step>
[Core idea]: We start by applying the change-of-base formula for logarithms to rewrite the equation.
[Full step]: The change-of-base formula for logarithms states that for any positive real numbers a, b, and c, and for any a ≠ 1, b ≠ 1, c ≠ 1: $\log_{a}c = \frac{\log_{b}c}{\log_{b}a}$. We can use this formula to rewrite the given equation using a common base. Let's use the natural logarithm (base e) as our common base. Applying the change-of-base formula to each term, we get: $\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{\ln 2023}{\ln (2023x)}$. We simplify the equation by canceling out the common factors of ln 2023 in the numerators and denominators of the fractions on both sides.
</step>
Step 2: <step>
[Core idea]: Simplify the resulting equation by using properties of logarithms to combine the fractions and potentially isolate the variable x.
[Full step]: After canceling out the common factors of ln 2023, the equation becomes: $\frac{1}{\ln (7x)}\cdot\frac{1}{\ln (289x)}=\frac{1}{\ln (2023x)}$. Simplifying this equation, we can multiply both sides by the product of the denominators to eliminate the fractions. This results in $(\ln (7x))(\ln (289x))=(\ln (2023x))$. We then apply the property of logarithms that states $\log_{a}b\cdot\log_{b}c = \log_{a}c$. This allows us to rewrite the equation as $\ln (7x\cdot 289x)=\ln (2023x)$. Simplifying the left-hand side gives us $\ln (2023\cdot 7x^2) = \ln (2023x)$. Since the natural logarithm function is one-to-one, we can equate the expressions inside the logarithms, resulting in $2023\cdot 7x^2 = 2023x$. Now we have an algebraic equation that we can solve for x.
</step>
Step 3: <step>
[Core idea]: Focus on the equality of the expressions inside the logarithms, leading to a comparison of the product of the arguments of the logarithms.
[Full step]: We begin by equating the expressions inside the logarithms: $2023\cdot 7x^2 = 2023x$. We can simplify this equation by first factoring out the common factor of 2023 from both sides. This yields $2023(7x^2) = 2023x$. The factor 2023 cancels out on both sides, leaving us with $7x^2 = x$. Now we have a quadratic equation in x. To isolate x, we can rearrange the equation by subtracting x from both sides, giving us $7x^2 - x = 0$. We can then factor out x from both terms, resulting in $x(7x - 1) = 0$. This is a product of two factors, and we can set each factor equal to zero to find the possible solutions for x. Therefore, we have the equation $x = 0$ or $7x - 1 = 0$. We can solve each of these equations for x by isolating the variable. For the first equation, we have $x = 0$. For the second equation, we add 1 to both sides to get $7x = 1$, and then divide both sides by 7 to get $x = \frac{1}{7}$.
</step>
